7
Discussion
The results and corresponding analysis opens for subjects to be discussed, hence overall
the tests did not clearly answer the problem statement.
7.1
Test 1: Test house
To understand and present the data, a lot of averages has been done. Thinking of the mov-
ing average, different methods have been investigated, all with a similar result. Therefore,
the EMA method is assessed reasonable for the later processing of data. Additionally, two
locations stood out looking at temperatures and RH. They were excluded from the further
work, because the circumstances are assessed uncertain. If the locations were a part of
the further work, the evaluations would be similar, since the overall shapes of the curves
were the same with or without them. Though, the concrete values would be influenced.
Extensionally, the averages within a subsections are mostly valued to comparison, since
the temperatures and RH are not weighted or relative to the volume, hence many sensors
are placed at the southern part, which might twist the results.
Even though the ventilation was reduced relatively much manually, the conditions in the
attics did not show clear signs of reduction in the results, like in the Master Project [12].
To reach a noticeable reduction it might be relevant to cover more of the opening at the
bottom of the attic as well. Additionally, thinking of respective extremes of temperatures
and RH it might be advantageous to perform the test in the summer and winter period,
or just extend the period of the test.
The range of MC spans from 7.0% to 17.3%, which overall is common in roof construc-
tions. Since the ventilation has been reduced, it was expected to possibly reach a higher
MC, but these values confirm that the reduction was too small to have an effect. In the
measurements of MC a limitation of 7% occurred, hence when the roof construction got
dry, the differences were impossible to measure. Though, the trusses might be stable at
that level, hence the temperature and RH did reach a stable level. During the measuring
period, the weather conditions change and got relatively stable, hence it might affect more
equal conditions in terms of RH. For the temperatures and RH conditions two locations
stood out. Location 1 and 6 are way different than the others, hence the sensors might be
covered by some materials, or affected by the conditions from the indoor.
The RH in location 4 at the peak of the attic as observed relatively high looking at M1.1.all.
Though, the variation is only approximately 5%, which is not considered as extreme in
relation to each other, hence this difference should not be enough for the PMPF to withdraw
only at the peak. Further, thinking of the relatively similar temperatures, the conditions
in the tests do not clearly state different conditions, hence not worse conditions at peak.
This might be of a larger difference in the winter with higher RH outside. Otherwise, it
Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters
75
==PAGE:84==
could be more extreme with more reduced ventilation.
7.2
Test 2 and 3: Joints affected by varying temperature and relative humidity
Small signs of withdrawal did happen in the two tests, but first, the conditions and per-
formance of the test are discussed. The circumstances the workpieces were exposed to in
test 2 were generally close to the setup. Only three days differed from the programmed
cycles, but it is assessed that the conditions in the three days were close to the range, hence
mainly the number of cycles was affected by the power fails. The cycles are assessed as
stable so the number of workpieces in the large climate chamber is assessed appropriately,
hence only the exact value of the conditions in the large climate chamber is uncertain. In
the test, it was assessed that the large climate chamber was calibrated, and movements
of the external sensor did change a bit on the values. Therefore, the location of the sen-
sors might be the difference. If the data from the external sensors are the correct value,
the workpieces would still have been exposed to a temperature variation of approximately
40℃within the same level of both temperature and RH. Therefore, the differences between
internal and external sensors are assessed for miner impact on the conclusion of the results.
Though, the cycles might not be suitable for withdrawal to happen. The cycles were set up
based on the capacity of the large climate chamber, hence the temperatures of the wood
and steel might not be reached within the cycles. Maybe, the cycles should have been
longer for the full extension to happen. A measurement of the surfaces would have been
preferred to confirm or deny this idea. Further, the workpiece could be measured in the
length direction to see if the materials change in length and if it occurs at the same time
and pace. Though longer cycles would have affected the number of cycles obtained within
the present project, hence withdrawal might need a high number of cycles.
Whereas the circumstances the workpieces were exposed to in test 3 only were partly as
planned. The workpieces did reach an acceptable level of MC at 50% RH, but at the
times with RH of 85%, the small climate chamber went out of order in terms of moisture
supply. In both cases, the RH ended way lower than 50%, hence the actual exposure to
the workpieces was more extreme in terms of low RH. Thinking of the high extreme of
85% RH the workpieces only obtained respectively below 60% and 70% of the target. The
curves had not flattened out, which indicates that more moisture could be obtained by
the workpieces. Therefore, test 3 only reaches the target two times at the low value and
not once in the high, hence not one cycle of RH change has been completed. Though, the
workpieces have been exposed to varying RH. Except for the total failures of the small
climate chamber, it seems to be stable over time, hence three workpieces were suitable
for the capacity of the climate chamber. Additionally, the opening when weighing of the
workpieces occurred was measured so small that it is assessed of a miner influence of the
conditions. The largest impact the opening could occur, where to extend the intervals, but
this time would be small thinking of the whole picture. Since the small climate chamber
is small, only three workpieces would be tested, hence it would be preferable to test more
76
Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters
==PAGE:85==
workpieces to evaluate on more general tendencies. Though, the small climate chamber
might not have the capacity for that.
From the results and weight measurements for the small climate chamber during the test,
uncertainties about the conditions in the climate room have occurred. It might as well be
the conditions in the climate chambers that are not calibrated, but the weight did change
even if the temperature and RH were the same both in the climate chambers and in the
climate room. The small variations are assessed miner since the weighing still showed a
tendency of the obtained MC of the workpieces. Though, it should be noticed that the
conditions that the workpieces have been exposed to might not be exactly what it was
set up to. These uncertainties spread to the calculations of MC, which were based on the
temperature and RH of the climate room. MC of the workpieces was measured a bit lower
than the theoretical values, but uncertainties also appeared with the measuring equipment
of the MC. Small misreadings or movements of the measuring equipment could make the
MC fluctuate both higher or lower. Therefore, the theoretical values were preferred. In
practice, the MC did not affect test 3, which was mostly dependent on the MC, because
the weight showed the same indications. If the curve of weights over time starts to flatten
out, the obtained moisture starts to reach the capacity at the specific temperature.
Withdrawal of the PMPF did happen for 5 workpieces.
The withdrawal was small in
all cases, but something happened.
It was not captured when, so it is open if it was
at the bright beginning or just before the test was stopped. The four workpieces from
test 2 had one thing in common: A small gap occurred from the beginning. The same
observation was made for workpiece 6 in test 3, which also had an extension of the gap.
4 workpieces were T-joints, while 1 workpiece was a length joint, hence it indicates that
fiber direction might affect the movements differently. Additionally, 4 workpieces were
categorized as high density, and thereby, the density might affect the withdrawal.
All
three types of PMPF were present for the withdrawal workpieces, hence withdrawal might
not be that affected by the type of PMPF. The observations regarding the information
of the workpieces are only assessed as indications, it only happened to 5 pieces, hence 16
other workpieces with, somehow, the same properties did not react to the same variation
of conditions. Additionally, all workpieces had a small gap as explained before, which
might be the strongest common influence. These observations verify that withdrawal can
happen in changing conditions, but not all workpieces with for example a gap had an
extension. 16 workpieces did not show clear signs of withdrawal. Some of these workpieces
were not documented from the right angle to see if the PMPF were punched into the
timber, and why it only relies on notes, hence some of these workpieces might have a small
starting withdrawal by moving from inside the wood to being parallel with the surface at
the end. Though the notes are reliable, hence it is assessed that 16 workpieces did not
have withdrawal. Since so many workpieces were not affected by the exposed conditions,
it should be considered if the conditions were extreme enough. Looking at the results
from test 1, it seems reasonable, but it might be worth expanding the range a bit to see
Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters
77
==PAGE:86==
if it forces the withdrawal to occur. Otherwise, a change of temperature and RH could
be combined.
Within the present project, the change of respectively temperature and
RH have been divided, so it would be possible to locate the essential parameter, but the
combination could be the essential parameter. Though, the movements that occur caused
by the temperature and RH might equalize each other. Test 3 might have the potential to
force withdrawal since the performance of the test was lacking and only three workpieces
were tested. The obvious reason that the withdrawal did not happen, is the time frame of
the project. Registrations of withdrawn PMPF are typically more than 10 years after it was
built. Maybe the small withdrawals are just the beginning. Lastly, the tested workpieces
were not loaded. It has not been assessed as necessary for the movements of the materials,
but it is a difference between the tested joints and the joints in attics.
78
Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters
==PAGE:87==
8
Conclusion
The test performed regarding ventilation has not obtained a large enough reduction of
ventilation, so it has been shown clearly in the results. Calculations of vapor pressure in
the three sections with different ventilation are relatively similar, hence the difference is
not assessed clearly and thus not assessed clearly reduced. Additionally, the conditions in
the three sections were generally similar only with small fluctuations. The main conditions
that stood out were located at the bottom of the attic, hence they might be affected by the
indoor climate. The MC of the trusses was within a common spectrum, which emphasizes
that the ventilation is good enough for keeping a healthy environment in the attic. Though
it did follow the temperature and RH and reached a stable level with them reaching a stable
level, hence if the ventilation was reduced to the conditions in the attic are affected, it will
also affect the MC. It is not concluded from the tests, that the peak is more exposed than
other locations.
The conditions in test 2 progressed relatively as it was set up to, which were 4-hour intervals
of changing temperatures between 20℃and 60℃, hence small power failures are assessed
miner thinking of the results. On the other hand, test 3 did not reach the planned setup
as the supply of water to the climate chamber failed, hence the workpieces did obtain MC
at a low level of 50% RH, but only reached up to 70% of the MC at 85% RH. Additionally,
drier conditions occurred when the water supply failed. The test could be repeated to map
the actual results from varying RH and thereby varying MC of the wood. Though the
tested workpieces were exposed to varying RH, hence the results are evaluated with the
consideration of the conditions in mind. Results from both tests show that the withdrawal
of timber joints connected by PMPF can be forced in an experiment. 5 workpieces showed
small signs of withdrawal after being exposed to respectively varying temperatures and
RH. 4 workpieces from test 2 with varying temperatures, and 1 workpiece from test 3 with
varying RH. When only 5 workpieces reach the withdrawal, it is hard to conclude generally,
hence the tests should be expanded and continued to get general tendencies. Though, the
5 workpieces that did withdraw had a gap from the start, which might be the key to
withdrawal from looking at the cases within this project. Not all workpieces with a gap
from the beginning expanded it, hence it is not a general conclusion. It is confirmed that
exposure to both varying temperatures and RH can force a small withdrawal of PMPF in
timber joints. Indications show that high density and T-joint might be more exposed to
withdrawal, while no clear signs of the influence of the three types of PMPF within the
present project occur. Withdrawal of PMPF for trussed rafters in attics might occur by
temperature or RH changes.
Withdrawal of PMPF have been registered in real cases, hence it does happen in trussed
rafters.
Indications in these cases confirm that extreme temperature or RH might be
causing withdrawal, which is verified by the tests 2 and 3. Though, it is not unambiguously.
There is a need of investigate conditions in multiple cases, and extend tests of varying
Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters
79
==PAGE:88==
temperature and RH to map the full problem of withdrawn PMPF.
8.1
Perspectives
The reduction of ventilation could be more extreme. The measurements could be made
over a longer time span, and especially at the winter with high RH or in the summer with
high temperatures. The data from BUILD contains much more results, which has not been
investigated with in the time frame of the project. Especially, the
It could be advantageous to register and systematize the problem since it has been hard
to force a withdrawal of PMPF. Then it would be possible to go more in-depth with for
example the case explained in appendix B, where similar circumstances seem to occur in
different houses. Measurements of attics could be made frequently, so these conditions
could be mapped or indications of extreme temperatures or RH occur in the problematical
cases.
Since the tests with the withdrawal of PMPF did not show any clear signs, tendencies, or
general behavior, it would obviously make sense to do more tests. As explained before,
it would be interesting to do test 3 again, where the MC obtains a higher value, and the
workpieces can be exposed to multiple extremes. Additionally, loaded joints might act
differently, hence a test with loaded joints could be made. Withdrawal of PMPF takes
time, hence further projects should contain enough time to develop the tests and hopefully
obtain a withdrawal of PMPF.

Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters

C
Registration note of metal plate fasteners in a garden
Case: Garden in Virum
Subject: Metal plate fasteners in a garden
Note formulated by: Benedikte Kirkegaard Breilev
Beds with metal plate fasteners, MPF, in a garden, which is in 2830 Virum in Denmark,
are investigated by Benedikte on the 17th of May 2022. The beds are erected about the
years 1985-1990, and defects are repaired continuously with a regular replacement of some
sides about 2000. Comments and experiences from the owner are added to support the
registration and its conclusions. The full correspondence with the owner is attached at the
end of the note in section C starting at page 93.
The MPF are used in the construction of 5 beds, which are located at one corner of a
garden. The garden is facing south/southeast, hence the sun points directly at the beds
almost all the time it is up. However, three trees provide shades along with the hedge
facing east. An outline map of the garden occurs in figure 76 below of which a shed also
occurs, hence it also provides shades to the beds close to.
Figure 76: Outline map of registered garden
The sun was shining at the registration day, why it was observed that the gab between
the hedge and the trees allowed the morning sun to touch the beds to a greater or lesser
degree. All beds were spontaneously hit, since it was through the leaves of the trees, but
especially bed A and B had more sun at this time of the day. Concurrently, bed D and E
Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters
87
==PAGE:96==
are most in the shadows. This day is assumed to represent most summer days, but the sun
might be higher at the middle of the summer and thereby not hit through the gap to the
same spots of the beds. Contrarily, the trees shade less in the winter, hence all beds do
get some direct sunshine through the winter. However, many sunshine hours occur in the
summer. The actual weather conditions and the beds in the garden occur at the pictures
on figure 77. The conditions and observations were later confirmed by the owner. The
specific correspondence with the owner about the beds occur at page 95. It is also worth
mentioning that during the afternoon and evening all beds are a bit shaded by the trees,
but especially the beds closest to the tree heading west, hence bed B and C. Bed A might
be free from the shades in the late hours.
Figure 77: Beds in the garden
The MPF is used for keeping timber pieces together that works as sides of a bed. At the
corners an angle bracket holds two sides together. The materials used to build the beds are
recycled. The owner had MPF in stock for free and the timber were remains from other
projects. The installation of the MPF is done by hand using a hammer to get the MPF
in the timber, which caused some irregularities of the MPF. Though, the MPF have been
fully pushed into the timber. The MPF gave signs of withdraw within approximately 2
years, and the repairs consisted of hammering the MPF into the timber again.
In general, the MPF are worn down at the time of registration, but they are also exposed
to all weather conditions in Denmark - varying temperature and relative humidity, but
they are also in direct contact with water and directly hit by the sun. The direct contact
is not standard recommendation for MPF which might contribute to the sign of corrosion
that most MPF had. Also, many MPF were withdrawn approximately 1-10 mm. MPF at
the shadows were generally more exposed to algae and less withdrawing, with exceptions.
The numbering of the beds occurs in figure 78 of which an overview of the withdraw MPF
also occur. The locations are approximations, hence the map should be read as a diagram.
Additionally, the circles next to each other are under and above each other.

Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters
==PAGE:97==
Figure 78: Outline map of beds
Bed A, B, and C are the only beds with observed withdraw of more than approximately
3 mm, hence bed D and E are only noted in the gap of 0-3 mm. Generally, the variation
of withdraw is larger at bed A, B, and C, since they span from 0-7 mm - and for bed B
it increase even further up to 10 mm. The side affected most of withdraw is the southern
side in bed B and C. Similarly, the south facing side of bed A have a large withdraw, but
the west side is the worst. The south facing side at bed A might be a bit shaded by bed
B, since the side of bed B is high and the space between beds are low. The withdraw on
the east side is of a similar size as the south facing side. The withdraws in bed D and E
are overall low, hence the withdraws are more random, but occur most to south and west.
Looking at the bed sides turning east withdraw is largest at the north, while it decreases
looking at withdraw to the southern part, hence roughly the same pattern as the observed
amount of sun hitting the beds with exception of E7. Also, bed B and C have the same
size of gaps against east, so it might be coincidental. Comparably, looking at the bed
sides turning west withdraw is largest at the north, but is lowest close to the tree. Again,
the withdraw might depend on the amount of sun hitting, but other factors might have an
influence as well. The gab size of the withdraw is generally larger at west than east. Again,
this might be influenced of the amount of sun hitting the beds, which is larger from west
caused by the hedge and locations of trees in the east, but this might not be the primarily
influence.

At bed E the MPF are not that withdrawn, since E1 and E2 are withdrawn approximately
2-3 mm, while E4 is 2-3 mm withdrawn only at the top. These three MPF are the worst
cases at bed E. E3 is close to the timber, which are affected by algae, hence it indicates more
shadows than sun even though some sun hit the MPF at the registration. Additionally,
the remaining MPF are mainly close to the timber or only small varying distances to the
timber. The small variations might be caused by irregularities in the installation of the
MPF, but the remaining MPF are also affected by soil and corrosion.
(a) MPF E1

Figure 82: Documentation bed E
Overall, the case showed that MPF exposed to extreme conditions can withdraw from
timber whether it is caused by movements in the timber or steel with changing temperatures
or relative humidity - or something else that has not been observed. It is important to notice
that the conditions of which the MPF are exposed to within this garden are a bit different
than in roof construction. Though, there might be indications of general observations. For
example, most of the critical or most developed withdraws are pointed to the south or west,
hence most exposed to warm from the sun. Additionally in the present observations, no
coherence of corrosion and withdraw was made and no signs of specific influence of growth
rings direction was made.
The information of the garden and thereby the registration note is based on the owners
memory and experiences, and the observations on one day. To make more scientific con-
clusions it will be needed to go more in depth with the actual conditions in the garden;
Measurement of the temperature, relative humidity, moisture content, and sun shadows
through the year, among other things.

Background of Jens Ljørring regarding metal plate fasteners
Questions, Q, and answers, A, between Benedikte K. Breilev and Jens Ljørring 11th of
May 2022:
1. Q: Hvad er din baggrund for at arbejde med tandplader? A: Havde i 70´erne stu-
denterjob hos et af de to førende tandpladefirmaer, hvor jeg kreerede beregningspro-
grammer til tandpladesamlinger – og spær generelt. Har i min tid hos DTI udført
prøvninger (til godkendelser) p˚a de fleste af de tandplader der er/var p˚a markedet.
Udfærdigede p˚a samme tid kravspecifikationerne til tandplader til anvendelse i DK
(MK-Godkendelseer). Havde gennem flere ˚ar en kontrolordning for tandpladerne,
hvor jeg rejse rundt til producenterne eller importørerne og udtog plader til kontrol.
Har siden været lidt ind over EN standarderne for b˚ade tandplader og præfabrikerede
spær. Havde igennem en ˚arrække den eksterne kontrol med spærfabrikkerne i DK
– først som en af Ingeniørforeningens godkendt kontrolordning som l˚a under Tek-
nologisk Institut, s˚a under Dansk Træcertificering, der endelig blev fusioneret med
Dancert. I disse ordninger var det udelukkende beregening og produktion spærene
de omhandlede, de tandplader der blev anvendt skulle være godkendte (eller senere
CE-mærkede)
2. Q: Hvad er din erfaring med tandplader overordnet? A: Rigtig gode. Er jo et genialt
forbindelsesmiddel til at samle spær i et plan.
3. Q: Jeg kan forst˚a, at du har været med til at introducere tandplader i Danmark – er
det rigtigt? A: Nej ikke rigtig!
4. Q: Hvordan foregik processen? Var det p˚a baggrund af erfaringer fra andre lande?
Hvordan foregik implementeringen i praksis? Blev lovgivning fra andre steder indført
i Danmark eller brugt som udgangspunkt til udformningen i Danmark? A: Tand-
plader kom vel fra USA, og havde været p˚a markedet i flere ˚ar i DK inden der kom
en egentlig godkendelsesordning.
5. Hvad var hensigten, at man skulle bruge tandplader til? Har de primært været brugt
til tagkonstruktioner eller har man brugt dem flere steder? Primært spær, men ellers
til alt hvor det giver mening – blev fx anvendt i enderne af jernbanesveller s˚a f˚a
ikke flækkede – Gang Nail havde et reklameslogan ”Never give e sleeper a chance to
split!”. Tandplader har ligeledes været anvendt til forstærkning af konstruktionstræ
Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters
93
==PAGE:102==
eller limtræ for at ”hjælpe” lidt p˚a forskydningsbæreevnen.
Vi bruger det selv i
laboratoeriet n˚ar vi skal have prøveemner gjort fast i diverse fixturer.
6. Q: Hvordan har dit videre arbejde med tandplader været? A: Har ikke arbejdet med
tandplader de sidste mange ˚ar – de var jo efterh˚anden prøvet alle sammen.
7. Q: Hvilke typer af fejl og mangler er du stødt p˚a gennem dit arbejde med tandplader?
A: Selve tandpladerne er der vel ikke noget problem med. Men montagen kan drille.
Dels er de svære at f˚a af hvis man har presset dem i et galt sted. Der finde specielle
”d˚ase˚abnere”, der kan rulle en tandplade af igen, men træet hvor pladen har siddet er
jo helt gennemhullet. Herudover er det vel fænomenet ”spring back” hvor pladerne
ikke presses helt i træet, men træet trykkes sammen af de tætsiddende tænder, og
”skyder” tandpladen op n˚ar samlingen tages ud af pressen.
8. Q: Hvad er de typiske fejl og mangler ved anvendelse af tandplader? Er der specielle
tandplader, som du har stødt p˚a problemer med – for eksempel med korte tænder
– eller bestemte mønstre? Hvilken type af byggeri er problemerne opst˚aet i? Har
der været særlige statiske forhold? A: Se ovenfor. Kan ikke lige minde at der er
systematiske problemer. Dog er der selvfølgelig (som din opgave nok er fokuseret p˚a)
at tandplader kan ”kravle” ud med tiden. Oplever normalt kun n˚ar tandpladerne
anvendes hvor de ikke skal anavendes, dvs udendørs, hvor konstruktionerne bliver
udsat for gentagne opfugtninger og udtørringer. I begyndelsen var der modstand
mod de korttandede tandplader, men det kunne ikke dokumenteres at de ikke duede,
s˚a de er stadig p˚a markedet i adskillige udgaver – 1 eller 2 tænder pr udstansningshul,
snoede tænder, pladetykkelser helt ned til 0,8-0,9 mm.
9. Q: Hvad er de typiske byggetekniske fejl ved anvendelse af tandplader?
Har du
observeret særlige vind og vejrforhold ved de typiske fejl?
Har der været noget
særligt ved ventilationsforhold for eksempel? A: Kender ikke til typiske fejl. Har
ikke set problemer – ej heller med korrosion, n˚ar pladerne alts˚a bliver anvendt til det
de er beregnet til.

med de sm˚a buler der nu kommer n˚ar pladerne er sl˚aet i.

oceaner af plader p˚a lager (gratis!!), og de giver en god plan samling.

at det generelt er et problem p˚a den langside og m˚aske det er startet før her/g˚aet
hurtigere? A: Rimelig antagelse – jeg har en enkelt gang forsøgt at banke pladerne
p˚a plads igen og/eller presse dem p˚a plads med skruetvinge. Men de er nok de kanter
der er udskiftet.

Appendix
A
Description of preliminary unscientific tests
Experiences are noted based on explanations by Finn Ehmsen who performed the tests at
the beginning of 2021.
Description of test
Overview: Two different cases were set up, the first case had ventilation for 16 hours and
heating for 8 hours a day, while the second case was ventilated for 23 hours and heated
for 1 hour a day. The idea was to create a reasonable circadian rhythm in wintertime, but
after the drying out of the workpieces, it was assessed that the heating affected the relative
humidity, RH, too much. Therefore, the test with 23 hours of ventilation was performed.
Additionally, the second test involves workpieces outside for comparison. Other than that,
the setup and method of the workpieces were similar.
Set-up: The workpieces in terms of timber joints were placed in an insulated wooden
chamber by hanging them to secure air between the workpieces, hence the workpieces
could be affected by approximately the same RH and temperature conditions. Examples
of the examined workpieces appear in figure 83, and the chamber is in figure 84.
Figure 83: Workpieces before test
Figure 84: Chamber

Performance: Hot air was supplied for 8 hours per day increasing the temperature to 60 ℃.
The last 16 hours were ventilated. The moisture content, MC, of the wood was examined
by weighing the workpieces, hence it resulted in an opening of the chamber. Also, the MC
of the workpieces was measured at the beginning, once during, and at the end of the test.
Additionally, pictures were taken of each workpiece so any withdrawal could be observed
and documented. These measurements were made continuously with 2-3 day intervals from
12.01.2021 to 09.02.2021 - the exact measure days appear in table 20 at page 98. The test
was stopped when the drying out occurred.
Measurements and results of temperature and RH: Data recordings of temperature and rel-
ative humidity were made during the experiment at intervals of 30 minutes from 12.01.2021
to 09.02.2021. The data appear in the graph on figure 85 at page 98. The conditions are
stable outside, while the conditions in the chamber are affected by the supply of hot air.
Once a day the temperature in the chamber increases drastically and at the same time,
the RH decreases drastically, hence hot air is supplied to the chamber. During the rest
of the day, the temperature in the chamber decreases while the RH increases. The slope
of temperature almost flattens out, since it almost reaches the outside temperature before
heating starts, and it does not get lower than the outside temperature. On the other hand,
most of the time the RH keeps a steeper slope, but it does not get above the RH of the
outside as well, hence the outside conditions are boundaries in the test. After 22 days the
supply of hot air changes, hence the conditions in the chamber get more stable.

The MC of the workpieces outside also occur, named U. The MC of U1 and U2 increase,
while U3 and U4 are slowly decreasing.
On the other hand, the development of MC
thinking of the indoor workpieces in terms of f2 and f3 decreasing fast, while f4 and f5
are decreasing slower. Lastly, f1 only decreases a bit. From the beginning, f2 and f3 have
a large MC in common, like U3 and U4 but they only decrease a bit, hence it indicates
that the RH inside is lower than outside. That might also be the reason for U1 and U2 to
increase. The workpieces indoors almost have the same MC at the end of the test, and the
workpieces with the largest gap of MC changes fastest. The close gap in the end results

A comparison is also made for the weights percentage of the outside workpieces and occurs
in figure 92. The tendency outside is stable hence the timber drying out in the chamber
must be caused by the contribution of hot air.

104
Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters
==PAGE:113==
Overall conclusion
Timber joints have been exposed to different RH and temperature conditions, while with-
drawal of punched metal plate fasteners, the weight of joints, and MC of the wood were
continuously observed. The tests were interrupted after approximately 22 days and one
month respectively since it was assessed that the wood was drying out, hence there were
no longer reasonable RH conditions.
Learning: This experiment is used as background to form the test to get an outcome, hence
a small guideline to indicate the prediction of the outcome. First, the experiment verify that
it might be possible to force the withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners to happen.
Though, the humidity needs to be controlled, so the moisture of the wooden elements
can be controlled, hence the wood keeps a relevant MC. Secondly, the time estimate of
withdrawal to happen might be at least one month or 22 repetitions of hot air, but this
is unsure since the withdrawal in this experiment might be caused by drying and not
repetitions of high temperature. The awareness of the relation between MC and weight is
taken into account as well as the methods to measure the workpieces. Further, learning in
terms of the opening of the chamber is not assessed influencing the results, pay attention
to noting data correct, and an example of handling data as a percentage of the original
weight.
Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters

Test workpieces: Growth rings
36 joints containing two wood elements fastened by metal plates have been delivered by
Palsgaard Spær. An additional documentation of all 36 workpieces in numeric order are
presented in the present appendix.
For each workpiece both sides with a metal plate
fasteners are shown together with close ups of knots and irregularities in appendix E,
whereas the growth rings occur within this section. The documentation is made at the
29th of March 2022 by the writer Benedikte K. Breilev at the Technical University of
Denmark.
The sequence the pictures are taken in of each type of workpiece occur in figure 93, hence
there are two pictures of the P-joint and three pictures of the T- and L-joint.

E
Test workpieces: Overview, knots, and irregularities
36 joints containing two wood elements fastened by metal plates have been delivered by
Palsgaard Spær. A documentation of all 36 workpieces in numeric order are presented
in the present appendix. For each workpiece both sides with a metal plate fasteners are
shown together with close ups of knots, flows/cracks with resin or other irregularities of
the specific workpiece. The amount of documentation variate from workpiece to workpiece
as the amount of irregularities variate, hence only irregularities are documented not plain
wood structure.
The documentation is made at the 9th of March 2022 by the writer
Benedikte K. Breilev at the Technical University of Denmark.

F
User guide to large climate chamber
This guide is specially made for the V¨oetcher climate chamber located at the Technical
University of Denmark. It is based on the original guide but is a more specific and extended
supplement to perform the exact test performed within this project. The temperatures and
relative humidity in the guide are based on the starting point of the test with the cycle
intervals in the following table 27. The guide includes a) set up for stable conditions at
the start of the test, which is done by manual work, and b) set up for the programming
of cycles to continue in 14 days. Before the start of the test, it is of high importance to
check that disinfected water is still connected to the machine, hence it is possible to control
humidity. Additionally, the machine should be turned on a minimum of 6-7 hours before
the start of the test.
Constant
Ramping
Constant
Ramping
Temperature [℃]
20
20-60
60
60-20
Time [h:min]
1:15
0:45
1:15
0:45
Table 27: Starting point of cycles intervals
F.1
Stable conditions from the start
Follow step 1-6 to set up the start conditions by using the manual work.
1. Press
to get into manual work mode.
2. To change the temperature to 20℃press on the button ’Temperature’, then the
screen change to editing, where the current value and edit value occur. Pressing on
the numbers to get 20℃and ’Edit values:’ change. End the editing mode using the
arrow. The editing mode close down and the ’Temperature’ button is updated with
the written temperature.
3. Turn on the humidity by pressing on the button
to the left. All installed
digital channels appear, hence the humidity should appear as well. Check that it is
turned on, or change it to ’ON’ by pressing on the ’OFF’ button next to ’Humidity’.
Close digital channels by pressing on the open door in the down left corner. The
button should now have one more green light like this
.
4. Set the humidity to 65% by the same method as the change of temperature. Press
on the button ’rel. Humidity’, press on the numbers to get 65 %, and end the editing
Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters
161
==PAGE:170==
mode using the arrow. The button should now have one more green light like this
.
5. Press on
second from the left to open the digital channels to turn on the
window air to avoid moisture on the glass. Press on ’OFF’ next to the ’Air flow
window’ to turn on the air flow. Close digital channels by pressing on the open door
in the down left corner. The button should now have one more green light like this
.
6. Let the climate chamber stabilize for approximately 30 minutes to the wanted tem-
perature and relative humidity.
F.2
Programming of automatic set up
The climate chamber can be automatized by using the programming. The description of
using the programming is based on the cycles below occurring in figure 202 and 203, which
should be repeated for 14 days.
Figure 202: System of the cycles
Figure 203: One cycle
162
Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters
==PAGE:171==
Follow step 1-7 to set up the settings of the climate chamber for the test.
1. Press
to get into automate work.
2. Copy an existing program to secure the back ground set up is correct.
3. Press on the edit button to edit the copied program, and choose an available spot
in the list of programs. The machine tells if the spot is free or not. Remember to
rename the program so it is locate the correct program later.
4. The edit-mode starts at the temperature.
5. Make sure to start the editing from the start of the cycle by clicking through all steps
with the left arrow. The arrow change from black to grey when it happens.
6. The first step of the cycle is with the conditions of constant 20 ℃in the time 1:15.
This is set up by choosing ’Prof’. The flat, constant line is then chosen. Now the
temperature and time of the temperature is chosen by pressing on the numbers, so a
small keyboard with numbers occur. Click the numbers and enter. Then you jump
back to the cycle.
7. The next step is the ramping. This is set up by choosing ’Prof’ again but then choose
the ramping development. The time and end temperature can now be modified to
60 ℃and 15 minutes.
8. Step 4-5 are repeated 6 times. The full time should then be 24 hours. Click on the
open door to exit.
9. When the program is done, you choose the program and click ’Start’. Be aware of
the conditions at the start, that you might prefer to be stabilized, hence follow the
manual steps.
10. After the start, the number of cycles of the program can be chosen. Click on ’Cycles’
and enter the preferred numbers. In this case 14, hence the program is 24 hours so
the test will take 14 days.

211
==PAGE:220==
K
Comparison of workpieces in large climate chamber
All 18 workpieces are photo-documented within the present appendix with corresponding
comments of gap and verification of the notes. The workpieces are ordered numerically
from 1 to 35.
Workpiece 1
The first side occur in figure 217, while the second side occur in figure 218 at page 213.
On the first side, the PMPF seems to have been punched a bit into the timber at the top,
and just to the surface with a gap smaller than 1 mm. at the bottom from the beginning,
which is verified by the notes. In the end, the conditions seem to be similar. The gap
might have extended a bit so the gap is 1 mm., but it is not measured hence it can not be
confirmed.
(a) Beginning, 09.03.2022
(b) End, 15.06.2022
Figure 217: Workpiece 1 at the first side
On the second side, the PMPF seems to have been punched into the timber at the top,
and just to the surface at the bottom from the beginning, as verified by the notes. In the
end, the PMPF is still in the timber at the top, while a small gap of approximately 1 mm
occurs at the bottom.
212
Withdrawal of punched metal plate fasteners in trussed rafters
==PAGE:221==
(a) Beginning, 09.03.2022
(b) End, 15.06.2022
Figure 218: Workpiece 1 at the second side
Workpiece 2
